# Soln

```python
class Solution:
    def subarraysWithKDistinct(self, nums: List[int], k: int) -> int:
        
        # if k == 1:
        #     return len(nums)

        def get_good_arr(k1):

            mp = {}
            j = 0
            c = 0

            for i in range(len(nums)):
                mp[nums[i]] = mp.get(nums[i], 0) + 1

                while(len(mp) > k1):
                    mp[nums[j]] -= 1
                    if mp[nums[j]] == 0:
                        del mp[nums[j]]
                    j+=1

                c += i-j+1

            return c

        a = get_good_arr(k)
        b = get_good_arr(k-1)
        # print(a,b)
        return a - b
```

# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Explanation: Subarrays formed with exactly 2 different integers: [1,2], [2,1], [1,2], [2,3], [1,2,1], [2,1,2], [1,2,1,2] ^GtgNR3LE

992. Subarrays with K Different Integers ^5K2YKxJ1

Given an integer array nums and an integer k, return the number of good subarrays of nums. ^efKbXQ9d

A good array is an array where the number of different integers in that array is exactly k. ^jRiyvzia

For example, [1,2,3,1,2] has 3 different integers: 1, 2, and 3. ^WW9qAevE

A subarray is a contiguous part of an array. ^A33TFJCU

Example 1: ^P2ZHQX4f

Input: nums = [1,2,1,2,3], k = 2 ^DTCJStwp

Output: 7 ^QLLLBpW6

Example 2: ^2ksHX1lf

Input: nums = [1,2,1,3,4], k = 3 ^pwxtjBe5

Output: 3 ^ZvBP7fgd

Explanation: Subarrays formed with exactly 3 different integers: [1,2,1,3], [2,1,3], [1,3,4]. ^0sQKlV6h

Constraints: ^7aYW4OMA

1 <= nums.length <= 2 * 104 ^gq1Z2FcR

1 <= nums[i], k <= nums.length ^gBmPcVsW
